vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">n</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math></p>



<p>This formula demonstrates that&nbsp;<strong>by reusing a nonce, recovering the private key is reduced to simple algebraic operations performed in O(log⁡n)O(\log n)O(logn) time, which is equivalent to a few milliseconds on a modern computer</strong>&nbsp;. It is critical to note that all the parameters required to calculate the private key<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">d</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>d, — namely<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">r</font></font></mi><mo separator="true">,</mo><msub><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">s</font></font></mi><mn><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">1</font></font></mn></msub><mo separator="true"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">,</font></font></mo><msub><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">s</font></font></mi><mn><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">2</font></font></mn></msub><mo separator="true"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">,</font></font></mo><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">H</font></font></mi><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">(</font></font></mo><msub><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">m</font></font></mi><mn><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">1</font></font></mn></msub><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">)</font></font></mo><mo separator="true"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">,</font></font></mo><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">H</font></font></mi><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">(</font></font></mo><msub><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">m</font></font></mi><mn><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">2</font></font></mn></msub><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">)</font></font></mo></mrow></semantics></math>— are&nbsp;<strong>publicly available</strong>&nbsp;on the Bitcoin blockchain, as&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/transaction">signatures and transactions</a>&nbsp;are stored in plaintext.&nbsp;</p>



<p>A practical example of implementing Shadow Key Attack in Python demonstrates the triviality of private key recovery:&nbsp;</p>



<pre class="wp-block-preformatted has-text-color has-link-color wp-elements-032156427bb934bd0458e91a82a59560" style="color:#4092c2"><strong>python:</strong><br><br><strong><em># Extracted from both signatures (same value) # Extracted from first signature # Extracted from second signature # Recover nonce # Recover private key</em><br><br><code>from hashlib import sha256<br>from ecdsa import SECP256k1<br><br>n = SECP256k1.order<br>r = 0x... <br>s1 = 0x... <br>s2 = 0x... <br>h1 = int(sha256(b"message1").hexdigest(), 16)<br>h2 = int(sha256(b"message2").hexdigest(), 16)<br><br><br>k = ((h1 - h2) * pow(s1 - s2, -1, n)) % n<br><br><br>d = (r * pow((s1 * k - h1), -1, n)) % n</code></strong></pre>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter is-resized"><img decoding="async" src="./Shadow Key Attack_files/image-16.png" alt="Shadow Key Attack: Fundamental Threat of Bitcoin Transaction Nonce Leak from EUCLEAK Mechanism via Extended Euclidean Algorithm Side Channels in YubiKey 5 and Infineon Microcontrollers" class="wp-image-7561" style="aspect-ratio:0.7368362561401169;width:716px;height:auto"></figure>
</div>


<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="shadow-key-attack---eucleak--------nonce">Shadow Key Attack Linked to EUCLEAK: Electromagnetic Side Channels as a Source of Nonce Information Leaks</h2>



<p>The EUCLEAK vulnerability (CVE-2024-45678), discovered by NinjaLab researchers in Infineon security microcontrollers used in the YubiKey 5 series, provides a practical mechanism for extracting nonce information via an electromagnetic side-channel attack. This attack exploits&nbsp;<strong>the non-constant-time execution</strong>&nbsp;of modular inversion.<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">k</font></font></mi><mrow><mo><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">−</font></font></mo><mn><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">1</font></font></mn></mrow></msup><mspace></mspace><mspace width="0.6667em"></mspace><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">m</font></font></mi><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">the</font></font></mi><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">d</font></font></mi></mrow><mtext> </mtext><mtext> </mtext><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">n</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>&nbsp;in the Extended Euclidean Algorithm (EEA) used in the Infineon cryptographic library.</p>



<p>The Extended Euclidean Algorithm computes the greatest common divisor (GCD) of two numbers and simultaneously finds the coefficients of the Bézout representation, allowing for the efficient computation of multiplicative inverses in modular arithmetic. Mathematically, EEA iteratively updates tuples of values.<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">(</font></font></mo><msub><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">r</font></font></mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo separator="true"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">,</font></font></mo><msub><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">s</font></font></mi><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">i</font></font></mi></msub><mo separator="true"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">,</font></font></mo><msub><mi>t</mi><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">i</font></font></mi></msub><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">)</font></font></mo></mrow></semantics></math>, where at each step, division with remainder and conditional updating of variables are performed.&nbsp;<strong>Time variability arises because</strong>&nbsp;:</p>



<ol class="wp-block-list">
<li>The number of iterations of the algorithm depends on the bit length of the input data (nonce value<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">k</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>and module<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">n</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>).</li>



<li>Within each iteration, conditional operations&nbsp;<em>(conditional branches)</em>&nbsp;are performed , the time of which depends on the sign and magnitude of the intermediate values.</li>



<li>Subtraction and comparison operations are performed a variable number of times depending on the specific bit values<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">k</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>.</li>
</ol>



<p><strong>These temporal variations, measured with nanosecond</strong>&nbsp;precision&nbsp;, manifest themselves in the electromagnetic emissions of the microcontroller during cryptographic operations. NinjaLab researchers used a Langer EMV RF-B 3-2 electromagnetic probe and an oscilloscope with a sampling rate of at least 1 million samples per second to record these emissions. The cost of the complete experimental setup is estimated at approximately&nbsp;<strong>$11,000</strong>&nbsp;.</p>



<p><strong>The EUCLEAK attack consists of three sequential stages:</strong></p>



<p><strong>The first stage is the acquisition phase</strong>&nbsp;: An attacker must force the device to perform multiple&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/transaction">ECDSA signature</a>&nbsp;operations using the same private key while simultaneously recording electromagnetic emissions. Obtaining a sufficient number of traces requires&nbsp;<strong>several minutes to an hour</strong>&nbsp;of physical access to the device.</p>



<p>​</p>



<p><strong>The second stage is offline analysis</strong>&nbsp;: The collected electromagnetic traces are subjected to complex statistical processing to extract information about the timing characteristics of the modular inversion. The researchers used bandpass filtering, moving median analysis, and correlation analysis to identify patterns associated with specific bits of the ephemeral key.<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>k</mi></mrow></semantics></math>By analyzing the differences in the duration of individual EEA iterations, it is possible to reconstruct the values ​​of the algorithm’s intermediate variables, which gradually reveals the nonce bits.<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">k</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math></p>



<p><strong>The third stage is the recovery of the private key</strong>&nbsp;: After partial or complete recovery of the nonce<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">k</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>from one or more signatures,&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/privatekey">private key</a>&nbsp;<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>d</mi></mrow></semantics></math>can be calculated mathematically using&nbsp;<strong><a href="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/shadow-key-attack">a Shadow Key Attack</a></strong>&nbsp;. If the nonce is recovered with errors (partial bit recovery), the researchers used&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/kangaroo">Pollard’s Kangaroo&nbsp;</a><strong><a href="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/kangaroo">algorithm</a></strong>&nbsp;to find the private key in a limited range of possible values. This algorithm for solving the discrete logarithm problem has a time complexity of<a href="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/kangaroo"></a><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">THE</font></font></mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msqrt><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">IN</font></font></mi></msqrt><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></semantics></math>, Where<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">IN</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>— a known range, which makes it practically applicable in the presence of partial information about the key&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptodeep.ru/doc/Biased-Nonce-Sense-Lattice-Attacks-against-Weak-ECDSA-Signatures-in-Cryptocurrencies.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">cryptodeep</a></p>



<p>The offline analysis phase takes approximately&nbsp;<strong>24 hours</strong>&nbsp;when an attack is initially implemented, but can be reduced to&nbsp;<strong>less than one hour</strong>&nbsp;with further optimization of the software and analysis methods.</p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<p>​</p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter"><img decoding="async" src="./Shadow Key Attack_files/image-17.png" alt="Shadow Key Attack: Fundamental Threat of Bitcoin Transaction Nonce Leak from EUCLEAK Mechanism via Extended Euclidean Algorithm Side Channels in YubiKey 5 and Infineon Microcontrollers" class="wp-image-7562"></figure>
</div>


<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="nonce">Lattice attacks and the hidden number problem: private key recovery from partial nonce leakage</h2>



<p>In a scenario where an electromagnetic side-channel attack (such as EUCLEAK) provides only&nbsp;<strong>partial information about the nonce bits</strong>&nbsp;(rather than the full value), the attacker can employ more advanced cryptanalytic techniques based&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/lattice-attack-249bits/">on solving&nbsp;<strong>the Hidden Number Problem</strong>&nbsp;(HNP)</a>&nbsp;using lattice&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/lattice-attack/">-based&nbsp;<strong>attacks</strong></a>&nbsp;. These attacks were first formalized by Boneh and Venkatesan and have since been widely used to&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/privatekey">recover ECDSA private keys</a>&nbsp;in the presence of side-channel leakage.&nbsp;</p>



<p>The hidden number problem is formulated as follows: Let the attacker know<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>d</mi></mrow></semantics></math>&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/transaction">signatures</a>&nbsp;<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>r</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mo separator="true">,</mo><msub><mi>s</mi><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">i</font></font></mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></semantics></math>for<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">i</font></font></mi><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn><mo separator="true"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">,</font></font></mo><mn>2</mn><mo separator="true"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">,</font></font></mo><mo>…</mo><mo separator="true"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">,</font></font></mo><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">d</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>, and for each signature it is known<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">ℓ</mi></mrow></semantics></math>high or low bits of the nonce<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>k</mi><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">i</font></font></mi></msub></mrow></semantics></math>This partial information can be represented as an inequality:&nbsp;<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">∣</mi><msub><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">k</font></font></mi><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">i</font></font></mi></msub><mo>−</mo><msub><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">in</font></font></mi><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">i</font></font></mi></msub><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">∣</font></font></mi><mo>≤</mo><mi>C</mi></mrow></semantics></math></p>



<p>Where<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">in</font></font></mi><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">i</font></font></mi></msub></mrow></semantics></math>— the known part of the nonce (e.g., the most significant bits), and<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">C</font></font></mi><mo><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">=</font></font></mo><msup><mn><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">2</font></font></mn><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">−</font></font></mo><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">ℓ</font></font></mi></mrow></msup></mrow></semantics></math>— the uncertainty bound for unknown bits.&nbsp;</p>



<p>From the ECDSA signature equation we have:&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptodeep.ru/doc/Biased-Nonce-Sense-Lattice-Attacks-against-Weak-ECDSA-Signatures-in-Cryptocurrencies.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">cryptodeep</a><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">i</font></font></mi></msub><mo><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">=</font></font></mo><msubsup><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">k</font></font></mi><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">i</font></font></mi><mrow><mo><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">−</font></font></mo><mn><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">1</font></font></mn></mrow></msubsup><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">(</font></font></mo><mi>H</mi><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">(</font></font></mo><msub><mi>m</mi><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">i</font></font></mi></msub><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">r</font></font></mi><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">i</font></font></mi></msub><mo>⋅</mo><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">d</font></font></mi><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">)</font></font></mo><mspace></mspace><mspace width="1em"></mspace><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">m</font></font></mi><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">the</font></font></mi><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">n</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math></p>



<p>Rearranging the terms:&nbsp;<a href="https://d-nb.info/1205171657/34" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">d-&nbsp;</a>nb<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">k</font></font></mi><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">i</font></font></mi></msub><mo><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">=</font></font></mo><msubsup><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">s</font></font></mi><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">i</font></font></mi><mrow><mo><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">−</font></font></mo><mn><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">n</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math></p>



<p>Substituting<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">k</font></font></mi><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">i</font></font></mi></msub><mo>≈</mo><msub><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">in</font></font></mi><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">i</font></font></mi></msub><mo><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">+</font></font></mo><msub><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">D</font></font></mi><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">i</font></font></mi></msub></mrow></semantics></math>, Where<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">∣</font></font></mi><msub><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">D</font></font></mi><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">i</font></font></mi></msub><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">∣</font></font></mi><mo><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">≤</font></font></mo><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">C</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>, we obtain a system of approximate congruences&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptodeep.ru/doc/Biased-Nonce-Sense-Lattice-Attacks-against-Weak-ECDSA-Signatures-in-Cryptocurrencies.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">cryptodeep</a>&nbsp;​:<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><msubsup><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">s</font></font></mi><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; <p>This system can be reduced to the Closest Vector Problem&nbsp;<strong>(</strong>&nbsp;CVP) in a lattice. The lattice is constructed<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="script">L</mi></mrow></semantics></math>with base matrix:&nbsp;<a href="https://fenix.tecnico.ulisboa.pt/downloadFile/1407770020547033/TESE-78314.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">fenix.tecnico.ulisboa</a><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mi>M</mi><mo><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; <p>Where<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">t</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>— a scaling parameter for balancing the sizes of grid components.&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptodeep.ru/doc/Biased-Nonce-Sense-Lattice-Attacks-against-Weak-ECDSA-Signatures-in-Cryptocurrencies.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">cryptodeep</a></p>

vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">−</font></font></mo><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">t</font></font></mi><mo><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">⋅</font></font></mo><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">H</font></font></mi><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">(</font></font></mo><msub><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">m</font></font></mi><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">d</font></font></mi></msub><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">)</font></font></mo><mo><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">⋅</font></font></mo><msubsup><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">s</font></font></mi><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">d</font></font></mi><mrow><mo><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">−</font></font></mo><mn><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">1</font></font></mn></mrow></msubsup><mo separator="true"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">,</font></font></mo><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">t</font></font></mi><mo separator="true"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">,</font></font></mo><mn><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">0</font></font></mn><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">)</font></font></mo></mrow></semantics></math></p>



<p>Using the LLL&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/lattice-attack-249bits/">(Lenstra-Lenstra-Lovász)&nbsp;<strong>algorithm</strong></a>&nbsp;or the more advanced&nbsp;<strong>BKZ (Block Korkine-Zolotarev) algorithm</strong>&nbsp;to reduce the lattice basis<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="script"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">L</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>allows you to find a short vector close to<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="bold"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">in</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>, from which the private key can be extracted<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">d</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>d.&nbsp;</p>



<p>The LLL algorithm has polynomial time complexity.<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">THE</font></font></mi><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">(</font></font></mo><msup><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">d</font></font></mi><mn>5</mn></msup><mo><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">⋅</font></font></mo><msup><mi>B</mi><mn><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">2</font></font></mn></msup><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">)</font></font></mo></mrow></semantics></math>, Where<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">B</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>— the maximum size of the basis matrix elements, making lattice attacks&nbsp;<strong>practically feasible</strong>&nbsp;given a sufficient number of signatures with partially leaked nonces. Research shows that recovering a 256-bit&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/transaction">ECDSA</a>&nbsp;private key on the secp256k1 curve requires:&nbsp;</p>



<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li>With&nbsp;<strong>2</strong>&nbsp;nonce bits leaked from each signature: approximately&nbsp;<strong>200 signatures</strong>&nbsp;.&nbsp;</li>



<li>With&nbsp;<strong>4</strong>&nbsp;nonce bits leaked from each signature: approximately&nbsp;<strong>100 signatures</strong>&nbsp;.&nbsp;</li>



<li>With&nbsp;<strong>8</strong>&nbsp;nonce bits leaked from each signature: approximately&nbsp;<strong>50 signatures</strong>&nbsp;.&nbsp;</li>
</ul>



<p>These results confirm that even&nbsp;<strong>a small leak of nonce information through side channels (such as EUCLEAK) can lead to full recovery of the private key given a sufficient number of observed signatures</strong>&nbsp;.&nbsp;<a href="https://fenix.tecnico.ulisboa.pt/downloadFile/1407770020547033/TESE-78314.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">fenix.tecnico.ulisboa</a></p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter"><img decoding="async" src="./Shadow Key Attack_files/image-19.png" alt="Shadow Key Attack: Fundamental Threat of Bitcoin Transaction Nonce Leak from EUCLEAK Mechanism via Extended Euclidean Algorithm Side Channels in YubiKey 5 and Infineon Microcontrollers" class="wp-image-7564"></figure>
</div>


<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="shadow-key-attack---bitcoin">Practical Applicability of Shadow Key Attack to the Bitcoin Ecosystem: Attack Scenarios and Threat Scope</h2>



<p>The Bitcoin cryptocurrency relies on&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/transaction">the ECDSA</a>&nbsp;algorithm with the secp256k1 curve as a fundamental cryptographic primitive for securing&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/transaction">transactions</a>&nbsp;and controlling ownership of digital assets. Each Bitcoin user generates a key pair:&nbsp;<strong>a private key</strong>&nbsp;<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>d</mi></mrow></semantics></math>— a random 256-bit number from the range<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mn>1</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>n</mi><mo>−</mo><mn><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">1</font></font></mn><mo stretchy="false">]</mo></mrow></semantics></math>, and&nbsp;<strong>the public key</strong>&nbsp;<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>P</mi><mo>=</mo><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">d</font></font></mi><mo>⋅</mo><mi>G</mi></mrow></semantics></math>, Where<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">G</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>— a generating point of the curve. The public key is hashed to create&nbsp;<strong>a Bitcoin address</strong>&nbsp;to which funds can be sent.&nbsp;linkedin<a href="https://www.linkedin.com/pulse/trying-attack-secp256k1-2025-sebastian-arango-vergara-s3fyc" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener"></a></p>



<p>When making&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/transaction">a transaction,</a>&nbsp;the owner of the funds must create a digital signature proving possession&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/privatekey">of the private key</a>&nbsp;corresponding to the sending address. This signature is generated using ECDSA and verified by Bitcoin network nodes to confirm the transaction’s legitimacy.&nbsp;<strong>Compromise of the private key means complete loss of control over all funds associated with the corresponding address, with no possibility of recovery</strong>&nbsp;.&nbsp;keyhunters<a href="https://keyhunters.ru/shadow-key-attack-critical-ecdsa-nonce-vulnerability-recovering-the-private-key-of-lost-bitcoin-wallets-through-a-nonce-reuse-attack-when-signing-transactions-allows-an-attacker-to-perform-simple-ma/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener"></a></p>



<p><a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/attack">The Shadow Key Attack vulnerability</a>&nbsp;poses a serious threat to the Bitcoin ecosystem in the following scenarios:&nbsp;<a href="https://keyhunters.ru/ecdsa-private-key-recovery-attack-via-nonce-reuse-also-known-as-weak-randomness-attack-on-ecdsa-critical-vulnerability-in-deterministic-nonce-generation-rfc-6979-a-dangerous-nonce-reuse-attack/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">keyhunters</a></p>



<p><strong>Scenario 1: Attacking hardware cryptocurrency wallets with vulnerable microcontrollers</strong>&nbsp;. Many&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/bitcoin">Bitcoin hardware wallets</a>&nbsp;use Infineon security microcontrollers (such as the SLE78 or Optiga Trust M), which potentially contain&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/attack">the EUCLEAK vulnerability</a>&nbsp;. An attacker could:</p>



<ol class="wp-block-list">
<li>Gain&nbsp;<strong>temporary physical access</strong>&nbsp;to the victim’s hardware wallet (e.g., by intercepting it during delivery or stealing it and then returning it).</li>



<li>Open the device and place an electromagnetic probe to record signals during signature operations.</li>



<li>Initiate multiple&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/transaction">transaction signature</a>&nbsp;operations by collecting electromagnetic traces.</li>



<li>Once sufficient data has been collected, seal the device and return it to the owner without any visible signs of compromise.</li>



<li>Extract partial nonce information offline within 1-24 hours using statistical analysis of electromagnetic emanations.</li>



<li>Use Shadow Key Attack or lattice attacks to fully recover the private key.</li>



<li>Create and sign&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/transaction">a transaction</a>&nbsp;that transfers all funds from the compromised address to an address controlled by the attacker.</li>
</ol>



<p><strong>Scenario 2: Exploiting Weak Random Number Generators&nbsp;</strong><a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/attack"><strong>(Weak RNGs)</strong>&nbsp;.</a>&nbsp;Some Bitcoin wallet implementations, particularly on embedded devices and IoT platforms, use pseudorandom number generators (PRNGs) with insufficient entropy. For example,&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/attack">vulnerability CVE-2025-27840</a>&nbsp;in the ESP32 microcontroller, used in some hardware wallets, resulted in the generation of predictable nonces due to a flaw in PRNG initialization. An attacker could analyze public signatures on the Bitcoin blockchain, identify patterns of nonce predictability, and use a shadow key attack to recover the private keys of affected addresses.&nbsp;<a href="https://keyhunters.ru/phantom-curve-attack-a-deadly-re-nonce-vulnerability-in-ecdsa-and-the-complete-hacking-of-private-keys-of-lost-bitcoin-wallets-and-exploitation-by-an-attacker-with-two-signatures-with-the-same-r-valu/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">keyhunters+&nbsp;</a>3</p>



<p><strong>Scenario 3: Side Channels in Cloud and Virtualized Environments</strong>&nbsp;. Bitcoin wallet services running on virtual private servers (VPS) or cloud infrastructures (AWS, Azure, Digital Ocean) are susceptible to CPU cache timing attacks. An attacker who has gained access to the same physical machine through co-location can observe CPU cache access patterns during&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/transaction">ECDSA signature operations and extract partial nonce information</a>&nbsp;using the&nbsp;<strong>Flush+Reload</strong>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<strong>Prime+Probe</strong>&nbsp;methods . This information is then used in a Shadow Key Attack to recover the private key of the hot wallet server.&nbsp;<a href="https://www.bitvault.sv/blog/cache-side-channel-attacks-on-bitcoin-wallets" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">bitvault</a></p>



<p><strong>Scale of real-world incidents</strong>&nbsp;: Research shows that Shadow Key Attacks have already caused significant financial losses in the Bitcoin ecosystem. An analysis of the Bitcoin blockchain conducted between 2017 and 2019 found that approximately&nbsp;<strong>0.48% of all&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/transaction">ECDSA signatures</a></strong>&nbsp;were affected by weak randomness or nonce reuse, leading to the compromise of&nbsp;<strong>over 1,331 private keys</strong>&nbsp;. In one documented case, attackers gained access to&nbsp;<strong>412.8 BTC</strong>&nbsp;(equivalent to over $10 million at the time of the attack) by analyzing duplicate values.<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>r</mi></mrow></semantics></math>r in public blockchain data. Automated bots constantly scan the Bitcoin blockchain for reused nonces, immediately exploiting any vulnerabilities discovered to steal funds.</p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter"><img decoding="async" src="./Shadow Key Attack_files/image-21.png" alt="Shadow Key Attack: Fundamental Threat of Bitcoin Transaction Nonce Leak from EUCLEAK Mechanism via Extended Euclidean Algorithm Side Channels in YubiKey 5 and Infineon Microcontrollers" class="wp-image-7566"></figure>
</div>


<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="nonce--rfc-6979---shadow-key-attack">Deterministic Nonce Generation per RFC 6979: A Countermeasure to Shadow Key Attacks</h2>



<p>The primary defense against Shadow Key Attack is to switch to&nbsp;<strong>deterministic nonce generation</strong>&nbsp;in accordance with&nbsp;<strong>RFC 6979</strong>&nbsp;, developed by Thomas&nbsp;<a href="https://www.researchgate.net/profile/Thomas-Pornin">Pornin</a>&nbsp;. This standard defines the procedure for generating a value.<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>k</mi></mrow></semantics></math>deterministically based on&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/privatekey">a private key</a>&nbsp;<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>d</mi></mrow></semantics></math>and the message hash<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>H</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>m</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></semantics></math>, using the cryptographically secure&nbsp;<strong>HMAC-DRBG</strong>&nbsp;(Hash-based Message Authentication Code Deterministic Random Bit Generator) function.&nbsp;<a href="https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc6979" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">datatracker.iet</a></p>



<p>The RFC 6979 algorithm works as follows:&nbsp;</p>



<ol class="wp-block-list">
<li><strong>Initialization</strong>&nbsp;: The initial HMAC-DRBG state is created using the concatenation of the private key hash and the message hash:<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mtext>seed</mtext><mo>=</mo><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">H</font></font></mi><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">(</font></font></mo><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">d</font></font></mi><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">)</font></font></mo><mi mathvariant="normal">∣</mi><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">∣</font></font></mi><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">H</font></font></mi><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">(</font></font></mo><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">H</font></font></mi><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">(</font></font></mo><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">m</font></font></mi><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">)</font></font></mo><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">)</font></font></mo></mrow></semantics></math><a href="https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6979.html" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">rfc-editor</a>&nbsp;.</li>



<li><strong>Nonce generation</strong>&nbsp;: An iterative HMAC process is used to generate pseudo-random bits, which are then interpreted as the value<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">k</font></font></mi><mo>∈</mo><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mn>1</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>n</mi><mo>−</mo><mn><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">1</font></font></mn><mo stretchy="false">]</mo></mrow></semantics></math>k∈[1,n−1].&nbsp;<a href="https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc6979" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">datatracker.ietf</a></li>



<li><strong>Determinism</strong>&nbsp;: For the same pair<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">(</font></font></mo><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">d</font></font></mi><mo separator="true"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">,</font></font></mo><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">H</font></font></mi><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">(</font></font></mo><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">m</font></font></mi><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">)</font></font></mo><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">)</font></font></mo></mrow></semantics></math>(d,H(m)) always generates the same value<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">k</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>k, but for different messages<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">m</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>m values<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">k</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>k are statistically independent and indistinguishable from truly random.&nbsp;<a href="https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc6979.html" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">rfc-editor</a></li>
</ol>



<p>Key Benefits of RFC 6979 in the Context of Shadow Key Attack Defense:&nbsp;<a href="https://hardenedvault.net/blog/2024-10-12-survey-oss-tls-rfc6979/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Hardened Vault</a></p>



<ol class="wp-block-list">
<li><strong>Eliminating nonce reuse</strong>&nbsp;: Since each unique message<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">H</font></font></mi><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">(</font></font></mo><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">m</font></font></mi><mo stretchy="false"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">)</font></font></mo></mrow></semantics></math>results in a unique nonce<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">k</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>, reusing a nonce becomes mathematically impossible (assuming identical messages aren’t signed, which is pointless).&nbsp;</li>



<li><strong>RNG Quality Independence</strong>&nbsp;: Deterministic generation does not require access to a source of high-quality entropy during signature creation, which is critical for resource-constrained embedded systems and hardware wallets.&nbsp;</li>



<li><strong>Compatibility</strong>&nbsp;:&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/transaction">Signatures</a>&nbsp;created using RFC 6979 are fully compatible with standard ECDSA verifiers and require no changes to the Bitcoin protocol.&nbsp;</li>



<li><strong>Testability</strong>&nbsp;: The deterministic nature of generation allows for the creation of reproducible test vectors, which significantly improves the quality of implementation testing and reduces the risk of introducing critical errors.&nbsp;<a href="https://hardenedvault.net/blog/2024-10-12-survey-oss-tls-rfc6979/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">hardenedvault</a></li>
</ol>



<p>Most modern&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/bitcoin">Bitcoin</a>&nbsp;implementations , including&nbsp;<strong>Bitcoin Core</strong>&nbsp;(since version 0.9.0, released in March 2014),&nbsp;<strong>Electrum</strong>&nbsp;, and popular libraries such as&nbsp;<strong><a href="https://github.com/keyhunters?tab=repositories">libsecp256k1</a></strong>&nbsp;, have adopted RFC 6979 as their standard nonce generation procedure, significantly reducing the risk of key leakage through weak randomness. However, older wallets, custom implementations, and some hardware devices may still use insecure nonce generation methods, remaining vulnerable to Shadow Key Attacks.&nbsp;<a href="https://keyhunters.ru/ecdsa-private-key-recovery-attack-via-nonce-reuse-also-known-as-weak-randomness-attack-on-ecdsa-critical-vulnerability-in-deterministic-nonce-generation-rfc-6979-a-dangerous-nonce-reuse-attack/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">keyhunters+3</a></p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<p>​</p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter"><img decoding="async" src="./Shadow Key Attack_files/image-23.png" alt="Shadow Key Attack: Fundamental Threat of Bitcoin Transaction Nonce Leak from EUCLEAK Mechanism via Extended Euclidean Algorithm Side Channels in YubiKey 5 and Infineon Microcontrollers" class="wp-image-7570"></figure>
</div>


<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Additional countermeasures: constant-time programming and physical protection against side channels</h2>



<p><strong>In addition to deterministic nonce generation, constant-time</strong>&nbsp;programming is a critical defense against electromagnetic side-channel attacks (as in the case of EUCLEAK)&nbsp;. This approach requires that the execution time of critical cryptographic operations be&nbsp;<strong>independent of the secret data values</strong>&nbsp;​​processed by the algorithm.</p>



<p>In the context&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/transaction">of ECDSA</a>&nbsp;, this means that the operations of nonce generation, modular inversion<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mi>k</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup><mspace></mspace><mspace width="0.6667em"></mspace><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">the</font></font></mi><mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi></mrow><mtext> </mtext><mtext> </mtext><mi>n</mi></mrow></semantics></math>, scalar multiplication on an elliptic curve<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">k</font></font></mi><mo>⋅</mo><mi>G</mi></mrow></semantics></math>, and the final&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/transaction">signature</a>&nbsp;calculation must be performed in the same amount of time, regardless of the bit values ​​of the private key and the ephemeral key.&nbsp;<a href="https://d-nb.info/1206005157/34" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">d-nb+&nbsp;</a>1</p>



<p>To achieve constant time in modular inversion, the following techniques can be used:&nbsp;<a rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank" href="https://d-nb.info/1206005157/34">d-&nbsp;</a>nb</p>



<ol class="wp-block-list">
<li><strong>Using an algorithm based on Fermat’s little theorem</strong>&nbsp;: Computation<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">k</font></font></mi><mrow><mo><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">−</font></font></mo><mn><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">1</font></font></mn></mrow></msup><mspace></mspace><mspace width="0.6667em"></mspace><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">m</font></font></mi><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">the</font></font></mi><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">d</font></font></mi></mrow><mtext> </mtext><mtext> </mtext><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">n</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>How<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">k</font></font></mi><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">n</font></font></mi><mo><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">−</font></font></mo><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup><mspace></mspace><mspace width="0.6667em"></mspace><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">m</font></font></mi><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">the</font></font></mi><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">d</font></font></mi></mrow><mtext> </mtext><mtext> </mtext><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">n</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>using fast constant&nbsp;<em>-time modular exponentiation</em>&nbsp;. This method guarantees a fixed number of operations regardless of the value<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">k</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>, but may be computationally more expensive than optimized variants of the extended Euclidean algorithm.</li>



<li><strong>Constant-time version of EEA</strong>&nbsp;: Creating a modification of the extended Euclidean algorithm where all conditional branches are replaced by bitmasking arithmetic operations, and the number of iterations is fixed and equal to the worst case.&nbsp;</li>



<li><strong>Masking and blinding</strong>&nbsp;: Introducing random values ​​that algebraically mask secret data throughout the computation and are then removed at the end, ensuring the correct result. For modular inversion, this might mean computing<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>r</mi><mo><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">⋅</font></font></mo><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">k</font></font></mi><msup><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mrow><mo><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">−</font></font></mo><mn><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">1</font></font></mn></mrow></msup><mspace></mspace><mspace width="0.6667em"></mspace><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">m</font></font></mi><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">the</font></font></mi><mi mathvariant="normal"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">d</font></font></mi></mrow><mtext> </mtext><mtext> </mtext><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">n</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>, Where<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">r</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>– a random number, and then multiplying the result by<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">r</font></font></mi></mrow></semantics></math>to receive<math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mi><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">k</font></font></mi><mrow><mo><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">−</font></font></mo><mn><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;"><font dir="auto" style="box-sizing: inherit; vertical-align: inherit;">1</font></font></mn></mrow></msup></mrow></semantics></math>.&nbsp;gistre.epita<a href="https://blog.gistre.epita.fr/posts/cyril.barbel-2024-09-09-using_side-channel_attack_to_extract_secret_key_from_yubikey_5_series/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener"></a></li>
</ol>



<p>At the hardware level, protection against electromagnetic side-channel attacks may include:&nbsp;<a href="https://www.unchained.com/blog/bitcoin-what-is-a-secure-element" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">unchained</a></p>



<ol class="wp-block-list">
<li><strong>Electromagnetic shielding</strong>&nbsp;of a microcontroller using Faraday cages or special metal coatings.&nbsp;unchained<a href="https://www.unchained.com/blog/bitcoin-what-is-a-secure-element" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener"></a></li>



<li><strong>Balanced logic circuits</strong>&nbsp;(dual-rail logic) that consume constant power regardless of the data being processed&nbsp;.<a href="https://www.unchained.com/blog/bitcoin-what-is-a-secure-element" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener"></a></li>



<li><strong>Noise injection</strong>&nbsp;into power and clock signals to mask information leaks.&nbsp;<a href="https://www.coolwallet.io/zh/blogs/blog/hardware-wallet-secure-element-the-complete-guide" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">coolwallet</a></li>



<li><strong>Self-destruct mechanisms</strong>&nbsp;that automatically erase private keys upon detection of physical intrusion or side-channel analysis attempts&nbsp;.<a href="https://blog.keyst.one/self-destruct-mechanisms-unique-defense-against-side-channel-attacks-4cfea3d4eff1" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener"></a></li>
</ol>



<p>Following the discovery of&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/attack">the EUCLEAK vulnerability,</a>&nbsp;Yubico released updated firmware version 5.7.0 for the YubiKey Series 5, which utilizes a new cryptographic library with a constant-time modular inversion implementation and blinding techniques. However, it’s critical to note that&nbsp;<strong>YubiKey firmware cannot be updated by users</strong>&nbsp;. The firmware is installed during manufacturing and remains unchanged for the life of the device. Therefore, the only way to mitigate&nbsp;<a href="https://cryptou.ru/bithorecover/attack">the vulnerability</a>&nbsp;for users of older models is&nbsp;<strong>to physically replace</strong>&nbsp;the device with a new version running firmware 5.7.0 or higher.</p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<p>​</p>
